<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><u><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Item 2.02&nbsp;Results of Operations and
Financial Condition.</font></u></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">On January&nbsp;25, 2006 the Registrant
issued a press release and held a conference call with analysts to report on
the results of operations for the fourth quarter of fiscal year 2005, which
ended on November&nbsp;30, 2005.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Furnished with this Form&nbsp;8-K as Exhibit&nbsp;99.1
is a copy of the press release labeled &#147;McCormick Reports Increase In 2005
Sales and Profits; Comments On Plan To Improve Business&#148;, which includes a
Consolidated Income Statement for the three and twelve month periods ended November&nbsp;30,
2005 and November&nbsp;30, 2004, a Consolidated Balance Sheet of the Registrant
as of November&nbsp;30, 2005 and November&nbsp;30, 2004, and an Consolidated
Statement of Cash Flows for the twelve months ended November&nbsp;30, 2005 and November&nbsp;30,
2004</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><u><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Item 9.01 Financial Statements and Exhibits.</font></u></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">(c)&nbsp; Exhibits.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The exhibits to this report are listed in
Item 1.01 above and in the Exhibit&nbsp;Index that follows the signature line.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><u><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">SIGNATURES</font></u></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Pursuant to the requirements of the
Securities Exchange Act of 1934, the Registrant has duly caused this report to
be signed on its behalf by the undersigned hereunto duly authorized.</font></p>

  <p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>
  </td>
 </tr>
 <tr>
  <td width="48%" valign="top" style="padding:0in 0in 0in 0in;width:48.02%;">

  </td>
  <td width="3%" valign="top" style="padding:0in 0in 0in 0in;width:3.7%;">

  </td>
  <td width="34%" valign="top" style="border:none;border-bottom:solid windowtext 1.0pt;padding:0in 0in 0in 0in;width:34.16%;">

  W. Skelton</font></p>

</head>

<body lang="EN-US">

<div style="font-family:Times New Roman;">

<p align="right" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:right;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">Exhibit&nbsp;99.1</font></b></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman"><img width="604" height="93" src="g35001mmi001.jpg"></font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt 5.0in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">FOR
IMMEDIATE RELEASE</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><b><u><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">McCORMICK REPORTS INCREASE IN 2005
SALES AND PROFITS; COMMENTS ON PLAN TO IMPROVE BUSINESS</font></u></b></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">SPARKS,
MD, JANUARY&nbsp;25 &#151; McCormick&nbsp;&amp; Company, Incorporated (NYSE:MKC)
today reported results for the fourth quarter and fiscal year ended November&nbsp;30,
2005, provided an update on the previously disclosed restructuring plan, and
announced long-term objectives as well as an outlook for 2006.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;text-indent:-.25in;"><font size="3" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:12.0pt;">&#149;</font><font size="1" style="font-size:3.0pt;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font><b><font style="font-weight:bold;">Increased 2005 sales and
earnings per share, overcoming several challenges during the year.</font></b></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;text-indent:-.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;text-indent:-.25in;"><font size="3" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:12.0pt;">&#149;</font><font size="1" style="font-size:3.0pt;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font><b><font style="font-weight:bold;">Generated significant cash
from operations of $339 million.</font></b></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;text-indent:-.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;text-indent:-.25in;"><font size="3" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:12.0pt;">&#149;</font><font size="1" style="font-size:3.0pt;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font><b><font style="font-weight:bold;">Provided details of the
Company&#146;s restructuring plan to improve sales and margins of its consumer and
industrial businesses.&#160; Charges related
to the restructuring plan reduced fourth quarter and fiscal year 2005 earnings
per share by 5&#162;.</font></b></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;text-indent:-.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;text-indent:-.25in;"><font size="3" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:12.0pt;">&#149;</font><font size="1" style="font-size:3.0pt;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font><b><font style="font-weight:bold;">Announced goals to grow
sales 3-5% and increase earnings per share, excluding special charges, 8-10%.</font></b></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;text-indent:-.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">Fiscal
year results</font></b></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">For
the fiscal year, McCormick reported $2.6 billion in sales, an increase of 3%
versus 2004, including a 1% increase from favorable foreign exchange
rates.&#160; Key initiatives driving sales
growth in 2005 included acquisitions, new products, improved marketing and
price increases.&#160; Sales from Silvo,
acquired at the end of 2004, contributed 2% to the sales increase.&#160; During 2005, net sales were negatively
impacted by several factors.&#160; First,
industrial sales were reduced by lower pricing of vanilla products and the
elimination of lower margin products in Europe.&#160;
Second, consumer sales in the fourth quarter were affected by the impact
of Hurricane Katrina on sales in the Gulf region of the U.S.&#160; Third, consumer sales of a limited range of
higher volume spice and herb items in France continued to be adversely impacted
by low priced products in alternative retail channels.&#160; The Company estimated that these three
factors lowered sales for 2005 by approximately 2%.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">In
2005, the Company exceeded its goal to lower costs by $25 million, achieving
savings of $33 million.&#160; These cost
savings combined with pricing actions, more than offset significant cost
increases in packaging and energy and the negative impact on gross profit from
the sale of products manufactured from high cost vanilla beans.</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<div style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><hr size="2" width="100%" noshade color="gray" align="left"></div>

</div>
<!-- SEQ.=1,FOLIO='',FILE='C:\JMS\msounda\06-3500-1\task766275\3500-1-mm.htm',USER='mssoundararaj',CD='Jan 25 13:12 2006' -->


<br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always;">


<div>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Earnings
per share in 2005 were $1.56 and included an $11 million charge (5&#162; per share)
for actions taken under the Company&#146;s restructuring plan.&#160; In 2004, earnings per share were $1.52 and
included a special credit of $3 million which was the net result of a $9
million credit (4&#162; per share) from a lawsuit settlement and a $6 million charge
(3&#162; per share) related to a 2001 streamlining action plan.&#160; Earnings per share rose as a result of higher
sales, an increase in unconsolidated income and lower shares outstanding,
offset in part by an increase in special charges, a higher effective tax rate,
an increase in interest expense and a decrease in other income.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The
Company continued to generate significant cash from operations, with net cash
flow from operations reaching $339 million.&#160;
This compared to $349 million in 2004 and $202 million in 2003.&#160; During 2005, McCormick used this cash and the
proceeds of stock option exercises to fund $186 million of share repurchases,
$86 million of dividends and net capital expenditures of $72 million.&#160; As previously announced, the Board increased
the quarterly dividend paid January&nbsp;20, 2006 to 18&#162;, a 12.5% increase.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">Fourth
quarter results</font></b></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Sales
in the fourth quarter declined 1% due to several factors affecting both the
consumer and industrial businesses.&#160;
During this period, the Company increased sales with the Silvo
acquisition, new products, more effective marketing and price increases.&#160; Demand for the Company&#146;s consumer products in
the U.S. Gulf region was lower due to the effects of Hurricane Katrina.&#160; Sales in France continued to be impacted by
competition from lower-priced products in alternative retail channels.&#160; Sales for the industrial business declined in
the fourth quarter due primarily to lower pricing for vanilla products and the
elimination of lower margin products in Europe.&#160;
Together, these factors reduced fourth quarter sales approximately 3%.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">In the
fourth quarter, gross profit margin reached 43.9% compared to 42.4% in the
prior year.&#160; Cost savings initiatives and
price increases more than offset cost increases in packaging and energy.&#160; Also reflected in this comparison is an
adjustment to the accounting in an industrial plant in Scotland that reduced
gross profit margin by 0.9 percentage points in the fourth quarter of 2004.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Earnings
per share for the fourth quarter of 2005 were 65&#162; including the impact of $11
million of special charges that decreased earnings per share by 5&#162;.&#160; Earnings per share for the fourth quarter of
2004 were 62&#162; including the impact of $4 million of special charges that
decreased earnings per share by 2&#162;.&#160;
Earnings per share rose as a result of an increase in gross profit
margin and fewer shares outstanding, offset in part by
a higher effective tax rate and higher interest expense.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">Restructuring
plan</font></b></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">To
further improve margins, the Company announced in September&nbsp;actions to
increase the effectiveness of its supply chain and reduce costs.&#160; At that time, the Company also disclosed that
a comprehensive review of its global industrial business was underway to
identify improvements. &#160;Following the
announcement, progress was made with both initiatives and in November&nbsp;the
Company&#146;s Board of Directors approved a comprehensive plan to restructure the
business.</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<div style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><hr size="2" width="100%" noshade color="gray" align="left"></div>

</div>
<!-- SEQ.=1,FOLIO='',FILE='C:\JMS\msounda\06-3500-1\task766275\3500-1-mm.htm',USER='mssoundararaj',CD='Jan 25 13:12 2006' -->


<br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always;">


<div>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">As
part of this plan, over the next three years, the Company will consolidate its
global manufacturing, rationalize its distribution facilities, improve its
go-to-market strategy and eliminate administrative redundancies.&#160; In addition, for the industrial business, the
Company will reallocate resources to key customers and take pricing actions on
lower-volume products to meet new margin targets.&#160; A new business-wide forecasting process is
being installed, and the use of technology will be accelerated to monitor and
manage the business more effectively.&#160;
Through 2008, these actions are intended to reduce the number of
industrial business customers and products in the U.S. by approximately
25%.&#160; Sales related to these customers
and products represent approximately 2-5% of industrial business sales in the
U.S.&#160; As these sales have minimal profit,
this reduction will lead to higher margins.&#160;
These reductions will also facilitate the consolidation of certain
manufacturing facilities which will further increase margins.&#160; As these changes are made in the U.S. and in
international locations, operating income margin for the industrial business
will increase.&#160; When compared to 2005,
operating income margin for the industrial business is expected to rise 2.5 to
3.5 percentage points by 2008, excluding the impact of special charges and
stock option expense.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The
Company expects that the restructuring plan will reduce complexity and increase
the organizational focus on growth opportunities in both the consumer and
industrial businesses.&#160; In addition, the
Company is projecting that $50 million of cost savings will be achieved by 2008
with at least $10 million to be realized in 2006.&#160; These savings will drive margin expansion and
fund initiatives to grow sales.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The
Company estimates that the total charges will be $130-$150 million.&#160; In the fourth quarter of 2005, $11 million of
these charges were recorded due primarily to the announcement in January&nbsp;2006
that two major U.S. facilities would be closed.&#160;
For the total plan, the cash-related portion of the charges will be $85-$100
million, of which approximately $60 million will be spent in 2006.&#160; The plan is expected to eliminate 800-1,000
positions globally over the three-year period.&#160;
A significant number of these employees have already been advised.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">Financial
outlook</font></b></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">With
strong business fundamentals and the improvement activities underway, the
Company set a goal for the next three years to achieve annual increases of 3-5%
in sales and 8-10% in earnings per share.&#160;
These goals exclude the impact of special charges related to the
restructuring plan and in 2006, stock compensation expense.&#160; As in past years, this sales growth will be
achieved through innovative new products, more effective marketing,
distribution gains and strategic acquisitions.&#160;
These increases will be offset in part by the negative effects of
actions to simplify the business, as the number of customers and products sold
is reduced.&#160; Sales growth and margin
improvement are expected to drive higher earnings per share as well as generate
funding for business growth initiatives.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">For
fiscal year 2006, the Company expects earnings per share in the range of $1.21-$1.24.&#160; This range includes an estimated reduction of
42&#162; per share for special charges and 11&#162; for stock compensation expense which
the Company will incur beginning in 2006.</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<div style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><hr size="2" width="100%" noshade color="gray" align="left"></div>

</div>

<br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always;">


<div style="font-family:Times New Roman;">

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">Chairman&#146;s
comments</font></b></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Robert
J. Lawless, Chairman, President&nbsp;&amp; CEO,
commented, &#147;In 2005, we faced a number of challenges.&#160; We have worked aggressively to address them
as well as reposition our business for improved performance.&#160; Despite these challenges, we were able to
grow both sales and profit for the year.&#160;
As we look back on 2005, we view many of the challenges as one-time
events and regard the year as a temporary setback</font> in our strong, long-term record of
business growth and financial performance.</p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&#147;We recently concluded a comprehensive review of our
industrial business.&#160; This business
continues to offer an important opportunity to develop and supply flavors to
food manufacturers and the entire food service industry.&#160; We have realized that we can better create
value by rationalizing our business and driving our products through fewer
customers, which will generate better margins.&#160;
During the next three years, we will eliminate underperforming products
and customers, reallocate resources to strategic customers, lower costs and
leverage our systems and capabilities.&#160;
These steps will lead to more consistent sales growth and profit
contribution from our industrial business.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&#160;&#147;Looking ahead, I am confident that the
significant actions we are undertaking will position us for future growth.&#160; The restructuring plan will allow us to
refocus our resources, continue to build competitive advantage and leverage our
global strength.&#160; We will improve the
growth prospects and margin structure of our consumer business and especially
our industrial business.&#160; Change is
always challenging, but I know that McCormick employees are up to the
task.&#160; I am confident that, as a result
of our actions, we will be better positioned to grow sales, improve margins,
achieve higher profits and increase value for McCormick shareholders.&#148;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">Business
Segment Results</font></b></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">For
the fiscal year, sales for McCormick&#146;s consumer business rose 5% versus the
prior year.&#160; Sales from Silvo, acquired
in November&nbsp;2004, added 3% and favorable foreign exchange rates added 1%.&#160; The additional increase of 1% was mainly
driven by pricing actions taken in 2005.&#160;
In the Americas, consumer business sales increased 3% with a 1% benefit
from favorable foreign exchange rates.&#160;
During the fourth quarter, Hurricane Katrina reduced product demand for
Zatarain&#146;s and McCormick products.&#160; This
had a negative impact of approximately 1% on the full year&#146;s results.&#160; The remaining increase of 3% was driven by
more effective marketing and sales of new products.&#160; In Europe, sales rose 10%.&#160; Silvo added 10% to sales, and foreign
exchange rates added 1%.&#160; Difficult
market conditions, particularly in France, continued to have a negative impact
on sales during 2005.&#160; During 2005, the
Company took actions in China to streamline both the number of products sold
and the distributor network to position us for growth in 2006 and beyond.&#160; As a result of these actions, sales in 2005
declined 3% in the Asia/Pacific region.&#160;
For the consumer business, special charges recorded primarily in the
fourth quarter of 2005 reduced operating income $10 million.&#160; This compares to $1 million of special
charges recorded in the fourth quarter and fiscal year 2004.&#160; Operating income was positively affected by
higher sales and progress with cost reduction initiatives during 2005.</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always;">


<div>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">For
the fourth quarter, sales for McCormick&#146;s consumer business were about even
with the prior year.&#160; The acquisition of
Silvo added 1% to sales, while foreign exchange rates had a negative impact of
1%.&#160; As mentioned above, the effects of
Hurricane Katrina reduced sales approximately 1% in the fourth quarter.&#160; The remaining increase of 1% was driven by
holiday marketing programs and new product sales.&#160; In the Americas, sales increased 1%, despite
a 2% decrease from lower sales in the Gulf region.&#160; Consumer sales in Europe declined 1%,
including an unfavorable 5% from foreign exchange rates.&#160; Silvo increased sales in Europe 5%, while
difficult market conditions, primarily in France, had a negative effect.&#160; In the fourth quarter, sales declined 7% in the
Asia/Pacific region due to the streamlining actions mentioned above.&#160; For the consumer business, special charges
reduced operating income $10 million in 2005, compared to a reduction of $1
million in 2004.&#160; Operating income was
positively affected by cost reduction initiatives.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

Business</font></b></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">For
the fiscal year, sales for McCormick&#146;s industrial business rose slightly from
2004.&#160; Foreign exchange rates added 1% to
sales.&#160; Lower vanilla prices in 2005
reduced sales 2%, and the elimination of lower margin products in Europe
further reduced sales 1%.&#160; However, these
factors were partially offset by increased sales of snack seasonings, and sales
to food service distributors in the U.S. and restaurants in the Asia/Pacific
region.&#160; In the Americas, sales rose 1%
with foreign exchange rates adding 1%.&#160;
In this region, lower vanilla pricing reduced sales by 3%, while
strength in snack food seasonings, certain new product successes and improved
sales in the food service distributor channel increased sales 3%.&#160; Industrial sales in Europe declined 5%, with
an increase of 1% from foreign exchange rates.&#160;
The elimination of certain lower margin products in this region drove a
large part of the remaining 6% decrease.&#160;
In the Asia/Pacific region, sales rose 7% with 2% from favorable foreign
exchange rates.&#160; Higher volumes were
achieved primarily with sales to restaurants.&#160;
Operating income decreased $8 million.&#160;
The sale of high cost vanilla beans during a period of declining prices
reduced operating income $15 million during 2005 and more than offset sales
gains in other parts of the business and the favorable impact of cost
reductions on the industrial business.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">For
the fourth quarter of 2005, sales for McCormick&#146;s industrial business decreased
2% when compared to 2004. Lower vanilla prices reduced sales 3%, and the
elimination of lower-margin products in Europe decreased sales 1%.&#160; In the Americas, sales were up slightly from
the prior year, with a favorable foreign exchange rate impact of 1%.&#160; Sales gains with products such as snack food
seasonings were offset by lower vanilla pricing that reduced sales in this
region by 5%.&#160; In Europe, sales declined
14%, with reductions of 4% from foreign exchange rates.&#160; The elimination of certain lower margin
products in this region drove a large part of the remaining decrease.&#160; Sales in the Asia/Pacific region rose
1%.&#160; Operating income for the industrial
business rose $2 million in the fourth quarter of 2005
when compared to 2004.&#160; In the fourth
quarter of 2004, the Company recorded an adjustment to the accounting in an
industrial plant in Scotland that reduced operating income by $6 million.</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">About

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">McCormick&nbsp;&amp;
Company, Incorporated is the global leader in the manufacture, marketing and
distribution of spices, seasonings and flavors to the entire food industry &#150; to
foodservice and food manufacturers as well as to retail outlets.</font></p>
